## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature, which is a fundamental problem in materials science where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic deformation laws and on temperature through thermal softening or thermally-activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon (combined linear and power-law response)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T)**c4 (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (coupled power-law in strain and temperature)
- Voce hardening with thermal effect: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal term)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Swift hardening law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (Voce-type saturation hardening)
- Thermally-activated flow: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation combined with hardening)
- Johnson-Cook homologous form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (with homologous temperature softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo-type thermally activated deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening with diminishing rate → Power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturation form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening of yield/flow stress → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or (T_melt - T)**c or exp(-c*T)
- Separable strain-temperature dependence → Product form f(epsilon) * g(T), common in Johnson-Cook type models
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Additive yield stress term: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon), where c0 is yield stress
- Thermally-activated dislocation motion → Exponential temperature dependence exp(c/T) in flow stress
- Strain rate analogy at constant rate → Power-law or logarithmic strain dependence mimics rate-dependent behavior
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as ratio (T/T_ref) or difference (T_melt - T) rather than absolute T
- Work hardening saturation → Asymptotic forms like tanh(c*epsilon) or c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation
